   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of missions to the Moon
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-move" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="50" height="20" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/50px-Mergefrom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/75px-Mergefrom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mergefrom.svg/100px-Mergefrom.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          It has been suggested that
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/List_of_lunar_probes" title="List of lunar probes">
            List of lunar probes
           </a>
          </i>
          be
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Merging" title="Wikipedia:Merging">
           merged
          </a>
          into this article. (
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:List_of_missions_to_the_Moon#Merge_with_List_of_lunar_probes" title="Talk:List of missions to the Moon">
           Discuss
          </a>
          )
          <small>
           <i>
            Proposed since October 2016.
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1270" data-file-width="1459" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg/220px-Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg/330px-Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg/440px-Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Surveyor_3_on_Moon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
          Surveyor 3
         </a>
         on the
         <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
          Moon
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luna_3_moon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="500" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/220px-Luna_3_moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/330px-Luna_3_moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/440px-Luna_3_moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luna_3_moon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The first image taken of the far side of the Moon, returned by
         <a href="/wiki/Luna_3" title="Luna 3">
          Luna 3
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As part of human
       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon" title="Exploration of the Moon">
        exploration of the Moon
       </a>
       , numerous space missions have been undertaken to study Earth's natural satellite. Of the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">
        Moon landings
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_2" title="Luna 2">
        Luna 2
       </a>
       was the first spacecraft to reach its surface successfully, intentionally impacting the Moon on 13 September 1959. In 1966,
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">
        Luna 9
       </a>
       became the first spacecraft to achieve a controlled
       <a href="/wiki/Soft_landing_(rocketry)" title="Soft landing (rocketry)">
        soft landing
       </a>
       , while
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_10" title="Luna 10">
        Luna 10
       </a>
       became the first mission to enter orbit.
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1968 and 1972, manned missions to the Moon were conducted by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">
        Apollo 8
       </a>
       was the first manned mission to enter orbit in December 1968, and was followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_10" title="Apollo 10">
        Apollo 10
       </a>
       in May 1969. Six missions landed men on the Moon, beginning with
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       in July 1969, during which
       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
        Neil Armstrong
       </a>
       became the first man to walk on the Moon.
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">
        Apollo 13
       </a>
       was intended to land, however it was restricted to a flyby due to a malfunction aboard the spacecraft. All nine manned missions returned safely to the Earth.
      </p>
      <p>
       While the United States focused on the manned Apollo program, the Soviet Union conducted unmanned missions that deployed rovers and returned samples to the Earth. Three rover missions were launched, of which two were successful, and eleven sample return flights were attempted with three successes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Missions to the Moon have been conducted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">
        European Space Agency
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
        People's Republic of China
       </a>
       . The Moon has also been visited by five spacecraft not dedicated to studying it; four spacecraft have flown past it to gain gravity assistance, and a radio telescope,
       <a href="/wiki/Explorer_49" title="Explorer 49">
        Explorer 49
       </a>
       , was placed into selenocentric orbit in order to use the Moon to block interference from terrestrial radio sources.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">
         Entered orbit on 28 August 1966. Failed to return images; other instruments operated correctly.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSC66_38-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-DSC66-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Conducted
         <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">
          gamma ray
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">
          X-ray
         </a>
         observations to study the composition of the Moon, investigated the lunar gravitational field, the presence of meteorites in the lunar environment and the radiation environment at the Moon. Ceased operations on 1 October 1966 after power was depleted.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
          <a href="#cite_note-45">
           [44]
          </a>
         </sup>

         </a>

          <a href="#cite_note-DSC66-38">

       <tr>
        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">
         Two tortoises and other life forms on board a technology demonstration for planned manned missions. Made a closest approach of 1,850 kilometres (1,150 mi) on 18 September, and circled the moon before returning to Earth. Landed in the
         <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">
          Indian Ocean
         </a>
         on 21 September at 16:08 UTC, becoming first Lunar spacecraft to be recovered successfully and carried the first Earth life to travel to and around the moon.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
          <a href="#cite_note-64">
           [63]
          </a>
         </sup>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">
         First manned mission to the Moon; entered orbit around the Moon with four-minute burn beginning at 09:59:52 UTC on 24 December. Completed ten orbits of the Moon before returning to Earth with an engine burn at 06:10:16 UTC on 25 December. Landed in the Pacific Ocean at 15:51 UTC on 27 December.

          <a href="#cite_note-66">
           [65]
          </a>
         </sup>

        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">

Spacecraft landed some 35 kilometres (22 mi) from the launch pad after successfully using its launch escape system.

         Intended to land on the Moon and return lunar soil sample. Did not reach Earth orbit after fourth stage failed to ignite.

       <tr>
        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">
         Intended to orbit the Moon and return to Earth. All first stage engines shut down 10 seconds after launch; launch vehicle crashed and exploded on the launch pad. Spacecraft landed safely 2 kilometres (1.2 mi) from the launch site after using launch escape sequence.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSC69_67-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-DSC69-67">
           [66]
          </a>
         </sup>

         </a>
         at 18:13 UTC on 14 August.

        <td colspan="5" style="background-color:#f0f0e0;">
         Third attempt at lunar sample return. After reaching
         <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">

         </a>
         , the fourth stage engine failed to fire for
         <a href="/wiki/Trans-lunar_injection" title="Trans-lunar injection">
          trans-lunar injection
         </a>
         due to oxidiser leak. Spacecraft re-entered Earth's atmosphere about 4 days after launch.

         . Entered orbit on 11 August 1976 and landed in
         <a href="/wiki/Mare_Crisium" title="Mare Crisium">
          Mare Crisium
         </a>

          96
          <span class="visualhide">
          </span>
          <sup>
           1
          </sup>
          ⁄
          <sub>
           2
          </sub>
         </span>

           [67]
          </a>
         </sup>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_missions">
        Future missions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_missions_to_the_Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Future missions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       There are several
       <b>
        future
        <a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon" title="Exploration of the Moon">
         lunar missions
        </a>
       </b>
       scheduled or proposed by various nations or organisations.
      </p>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Funded">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>

         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Late 2018
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
          <a href="#cite_note-135">
           [134]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         Two private citizens on a lunar fly-by.
         <br/>
         <p>
          The plan to use a
          <a href="/wiki/Falcon_Heavy" title="Falcon Heavy">
           Falcon Heavy
          </a>
          for this was abandoned in February 2018, immediately before the first Falcon Heavy test launch, in favour of a possible mission on the successor
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Falcon_Rocket" title="Big Falcon Rocket">
           Big Falcon Rocket
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
           <a href="#cite_note-136">
            [135]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

             <i>
              MoonEx's machines are designed to look for materials that are scarce on Earth but found in everything from a Toyota Prius car battery to guidance systems on cruise missiles. ... The company is among several teams hoping to someday win the Google Lunar X Prize competition, a $30-million race to the Moon in which a privately-funded team must successfully place a robot on the Moon's surface and have it explore at least 1/3 of a mile. It also must transmit high definition video and images back to Earth before 2016. ... should be ready to land on the lunar surface by 2013
